Дигитална дипломатија: функционалност на глобалното опкружување во дигиталната ера

Вовед во дигиталната дипломатија

Дипломатијата долго време беше сметана за уметност во спроведување на пре-

говори помеѓу нациите и начин на развивање на меѓународните односи (Baylis,

Owens, & Smith, 2017). Традиционално гледано, дипломатијата вклучува соста-

ноци лице-в-лице, пишана документација и кореспонденција, како и размена на

официјални документи. Денеска, со брзиот продор и развојот на нови технологии

и нови начини на функционирање на општествата, дигиталното доба воведе нови

начини на кои функционира и дипломатијата.

Во дигиталната ера, дипломатијата може да биде дефинирана и како употреба на

технологија и дигитални алатки во олесну-

вањето на комуникациите, преговорите и

градењето на консензус помеѓу држави-

те. Дигиталната дипломатија вклучува и

размена на информации, идеи и политики

преку различен вид на дигитални канали,

вклучувајќи и електронска пошта, видео-

конференциска врска, социјалните мре-

жи и on-line платформите.

Дигиталната трансформација, всушност,

во голема мера го прошири опсегот и до-

стрелот на дипломатијата, и им овозможи

на дипломатите да имаат пристап до по-

широки публики и поефикасно и Слика 3: Придобивки наспроти

поефективно да ги спроведуваат дипло- недостатоци за дипломатијата

матските активности (Melissen, 2017). од дигиталната ера

Дигиталната трансформација ја промени и динамиката во меѓународните односи

како и дипломатската практика. Една од најзабележителните промени е – брзина-

та и едноставноста на комуникацијата. Дигиталните алатки ги елиминираа стеги-

те на физичките дистанци и временските зони, и им овозможија на дипломатите

да разговараат во реално време од едната до другата страна на земјината топка и

инстантно да добиваат информации на глобално ниво. Тоа, пак, овозможува брзо

донесување на одлуки и забрзан ритам при споредување на преговори од секаков

тип (Fischer-Ontrup, 2019).

Дигиталната ера овозможува и друга многу важна придобивка, а тоа е демократи-

зацијата на дипломатијата, преку воспоставување на платформа која овозможува

поширок опсег на стеикхолдери да имаат можност да бидат вклучени во дипло-

матскиот дискурс. Преку социјалните мрежи, дипломатите можат многу лесно да

воспостават контакт со јавноста, со организациите од невладиниот сектор, со недр-

жавните актери, а сето ова овозможува дипломатскиот процес да биде потранспа-

рентен и поинклузивен. Сето ова значи дека дипломатијата е подостапна и поотво-

рена за интересите и забелешките на различни заедници (Slaughter, 2018).

Технологијата овозможи и развој на т.н. дипломатија базирана на податоци, особе-

но имајќи предвид дека дипломатите одеднаш имаат можност да извршат анализа

и да имаат увид во глобалните трендови, јавното мислење и мислењето околу тоа

кој е приоритетот во доменот на политиките, токму користејќи ги новите технолош-

ки алатки. На тој начин, дипломатите можат да донесат вистински одлуки, да ги

предвидат промените, да препознаат предизвици и да ги променат дипломатски-

те стратегии и тактики согласно овие правци. На овој начин, кажано со еден збор,

дипломатијата станува наука базирана на факти и докази, таа е проактивна, спро-

ведува ефикасни политики и овозможува поедноставен процес за окончување на

конфликти (Bjola & Holmes, 2019).

Дигиталната ера донесе и нови можности, но и нови предизвици – особено во до-

менот на сајбер-безбедноста и информациското војување. Дипломатите доколку

сакаат да ги користат бенефитите на технолошките изуми, мора да имаат начин да

се справат со комплексноста на сајбер- домејнот, да се осигураат дека информа-

циите кои се сензитивни се и заштитени и да бидат проактивни во справувањето со

дезинформациите со кои општествата се соочуваат секојдневно. Сето ова побару-

ва развој на еден робустен систем за сајбер безбедност со свои протоколи, додека

истовремено побарува и висок степен на дигитална писменост кај дипломатите,

кои сега мораат ефективно да се справуваат и со овие галопирачки закани во ди-

гиталниот простор (Cavelty, 2020).

Сублимирано, дигиталната ера ја трансформираше дипломатијата, го зголеми на-

чинот на кој истата ја дефинираме и ги редефинираше нејзините практики. Упо-

требата на сето она што денеска технологијата го овозможува ја револуционизи-

раше комуникацијата и инклузивноста, а го поддржа и процесот на донесување на

одлуки. Брзиот напредок на технологијата, пак, доведе и до појава на предизвици,

особено во контекст на безбедноста во сајбер-просторот, предизвици на кои ди-

пломатите мораат да се прилагодат, додека истовремено го користат потенцијалот

кој го нуди новото време.

Дигитална дипломатија: функционалност на глобалното опкружување во дигиталната ера

Важноста и користа од дигиталната дипломатија

Дигиталната дипломатија, позната и како е-дипломатија или сајбер- дипломатија

е новиот и модерен пристап кон дипломатската практика развивана со векови. Таа

претставува и витална алатка за владите и меѓународните организации. Како што е

наведено погоре, технологијата драстично го промени начинот на комуницирање,

а со тоа и ликот на глобалното опкружување. Едноставно кажано, технологијата

ја намали дистанцата помеѓу владите, дипломатите и граѓаните на светско ниво и

овозможи дури и директен контакт помеѓу нив.

Многу значајна корист од дигиталната дипломатија и новото време има во доменот

на кризниот менаџмент и окончувањето на конфликтите, особено затоа што во вре-

ме на криза или конфликт, пристапот до брзи и точни информации е од круцијал-

но значење. Преку дигиталните канали, дипломатите добиваат новости во реално

време, потоа споделуваат информации и ги координираат напорите на ефикасен

начин. Социјалните мрежи се исто така важен сегмент, особено кога станува збор

за брз трансфер на информации до крајните корисници – дали во форма на ин-

струкции за заштита на животот и имотите, или во однос на насоки за справување

со потенцијални закани.

Дигиталната дипломатија ја револуционизираше и културната размена, рушејќи ги

бариерите помеѓу различни народи и култури. Преку on-line платформите, владите

можат да го претстават богатото наследство на своите земји, својата музика, умет-

ност, своите традиции до глобалните публики. Сето ова не само што промовира

културна разновидност, туку го унапредува и меѓусебното разбирање и почит. Пре-

ку овие дигитални платформи можат да се промовираат и програми за изучување

на јазици и иницијативи во областа на образованието што води кон еден поинклу-

зивен и поповрзан свет.

Придобивките јасно можат да се видат и во доменот на економската дипломатија

и дипломатските иновации. Преку дигитални платформи, владите можат да при-

влечат странски инвеститори, да го промовираат туризмот, трговијата, како и да

го покажат својот економски потенцијал. Дигиталните алатки и технологии нудат

и нови иновативни решенија за глобални проблеми како климатските промени,

здравствените предизвици и слично. Заедничките напори, овозможени и од on-line

платформите кои служат како катализатор, овозможуваат развој на нови политики

и процедури кои се насочени кон изнаоѓање на решенија на овие прашања и пре-

дизвици.

Главните концепти и алатки на дигиталната дипломатија

Дигиталната дипломатија во себе вклучува повеќе алатки и концепти кои ги вклу-

чуваат карактеристиките на оваа гранка на дипломатијата.

Една од нив е и јавната дипломатија, која ги вклучува напорите на владите или ор-

ганизациите да пристапат кон странски публики со цел да изградат поблиски од-

носи и да промовираат позитивен имиџ за нивната земја или организација. Јавната

дипломатија може да се смета и за составен дел или сегмент на стратешките кому-

никации со намера да се влијае на јавното мислење и екстерната перцепција за да

се постигне одредена цел во надворешната политика.

Слика 4: Активности и алатки во доменот на јавната дипломатија

Главната цел на јавната дипломатија е да го унапреди разбирањето и доверба-

та како и добрата волја помеѓу нациите и организациите преку дисеминација на

информации, поблиска и посеопфатна културна размена и дијалог. Таа вклучува

различни активности како културни изложби, образовни размени, меѓународно

пренесување на содржини со позитивен импакт, настани со јавно говорење и спро-

ведување на дигитална дипломатија преку on-line платформите.

Јавната дипломатија се разликува од традиционалната дипломатија по тоа што

примарно не се однесува на интеракции помеѓу влади и официјални претставни-

ци, туку на развој на позитивни односи со недржавни актери, организации од не-

владиниот сектор, граѓани, медиуми, креатори на јавно мислење и слично. Јавната

Дигитална дипломатија: функционалност на глобалното опкружување во дигиталната ера

дипломатија ја препознава силата на јавното мислење и невладините движења во

обликувањето на меѓународните односи и токму затоа тие се нејзината цел.

„Де факто“, јавната дипломатија игра исклучително значајна улога во обликување-

то на јавната перцепција за политиките, вредностите и културата на една држава

и нација. Таа може да ја зголеми „меката сила“ на една држава и нејзината моќ за

влијание преку убедување, наспроти преку присилување. Со промовирањето на

дијалог, разбирање и меѓусебна почит, јавната дипломатија креира мостови кои ги

поврзуваат различните култури, ги решава недоразбирањата и промовира побли-

ски односи помеѓу државите.

Големо влијание врз дигиталната дипломатија имаат и социјалните мрежи како

Facebook, Twitter, Instagram и LinkedIn, особено затоа што дипломатите ги кори-

стат овие платформи за да промовираат мислења, идеи и политики и да иницираат

дискусии со оние кои ги следат. Комуникациите со дипломатите едноставно кажа-

но немаат граница, освен стандардите на дипломатската практика и етикецијата.

Најчесто, овој тип на интеракции и дијалог може да се види во односите помеѓу ди-

пломатите и претставниците на медиумите, експертите или т.н. „влијателни лица“

(анг. influencers).

Друга форма или алатка на дигиталната дипломатија е т.н. „дигитално раскажу-

вање“, зашто дигиталната сфера остава огромен простор за раскажување на една

совршена приказна за својата земја, култура или нација. Дигиталниот простор овоз-

можува користење на мултимедијални содржини како фотографии, видеа, инфо-

графици, подкасти, блогови и слично, со чија помош можат да се развија примамли-

ви и визуелно поддржани наративи кои предизвикуваат емоција и примамливост.

Дигиталното раскажување е уште еден посеопфатен начин за промовирање на

дипломатски пораки кои го задржуваат вниманието и интересот на публиката.

E-дипломатијата, гледана како алатка во суштина го опишува начинот на кој ди-

пломатската пракса се реализира преку новите технологии. Тоа вклучува алатки за

организација на on-line преговори, дигитални конференции, виртуелни самити или

безбедни конференциски врски за трансфер на сензитивни информации.

Една исклучително важна алатка за дипломатите е можноста за анализа на огро-

мен квантум на информации достапни во сајбер-просторот. На тој начин диплома-

тите можат да добијат слика за јавното мислење дома и во која било странска земја

и соодветно на тоа да ги променат или обликуваат своите дипломатски стратегии,

да ги идентификуваат стеикхолдерите, да го максимизираат ефектот на пораките

и најефикасно да таргетираат специфични клучни публики.

On-line кампањите се уште една стратешка алатка на дипломатите, особено кога

станува збор за таргетирано промовирање на политики, за справување со дезин-

формации и за подигнување на свесноста кај јавноста за одредени специфични

прашања. Дипломатските мисии можат да се вклучат во кампањи на социјалните

мрежи, во различни on-line петиции или различни локални или помали движења

кои можат да имаат национален ефект – и сето тоа со цел добивање на уште пого-

лема јавна поддршка.

Обуките за дипломатија спроведени on-line, се алатка која е од значење за диги-

талната дипломатија, имајќи ја предвид ефикасноста и брзината во спроведување-

то на ваков вид на обуки. Овие програми вклучуваат on-line курсеви, вебинари и

виртуелни работилници кои покриваат различни аспекти од дигиталната диплома-

тија, вклучувајќи и менаџирањето на социјалните мрежи, комуникациските страте-

гии во сајбер-просторот или кризниот менаџмент.

Улогата на социјалните мрежи во дипломатијата

Со развојот на мас-медиумите и мас-комуникацијата, социјалните мрежи рапидно

ги трансформираа не само нашите социјални животи, туку и политичките односи

и релации. Она што е јасно забележливо е дека во оваа модерна ера, политичките

лидери и дипломатите на глобално ниво сè повеќе ги користат социјалните мрежи

за да пренесат одредена политичка порака, да сигнализираат одредена политичка

намера или да се поврзат со одреден странски политичар. Доколку во одредена

ситуација традиционалната (лице-в-лице) дипломатија е лимитирана, социјалните

мрежи можат да бидат исклучително значајни во отворањето на дијалог и развојот

на довербата помеѓу државите. Во суштина, доколку се изврши анализа на начи-

нот на кој се однесуваат официјалните лица на социјалните мрежи, лесно се доаѓа

до заклучок дека нивните пораки упатени преку овие мрежи се конзистентни и во

рамката на тоа како една змеја сака да биде препознаена на меѓународната сцена.

Една илустрација за тоа е улогата на Twitter во донесувањето на иранскиот нукле-

арен договор. По прекинувањето на дипломатските односи помеѓу САД и Иран во

1980 година, потенцијалот за високо-профилни дипломатски интеракции бил мно-

гу мал, па затоа успешното донесување на Иранскиот нуклеарен договор во 2015

година претставуваше изненадување кое во одреден процент својот успех треба

да го припише и на социјалната мрежа Twitter. Имено, токму начинот на кој била

користена оваа социјална мрежа од страна на официјалните ирански претставни-

ци, овозможила да се создаде позитивна клима која навестувала поместување

од непријателските позиции, реконструирање на наративите помеѓу двете земји и

според тоа воведување на нови преговарачки позиции.

DigitalTransformation and Cyber Security

What digital transformation entails on a global level?

To understand the role of technological progress and digitization in today's society

we must go back to the very beginnings. The launch of the Russian Sputnik in 1957 is

probably the initial capsule for a more serious investment in technological inventions

and technological development that was evident in the sixties of the last century.

Sputnik, in fact, started the struggle between countries to possess, that is, to achieve

technological supremacy.

Social development has always been based on the value of knowledge, something that

is particularly visible today considering that new technologies are breaking down the

barriers of physical space, especially when it comes to the exchange of information

and data. Knowledge becomes a kind of collective good that works to improve socio-

economic development at the societal level.

Digital transformation is considered a new phenomenon, because this process has

recently gained popularity, although the "de facto" idea of offering digital products, or

rather, digital services existed as early as the nineties of the last century, and especially

in the period of 2000 – 2015 year. This period is important because of the wide spread

of smart devices and social networks that led to a drastic change in the way consumers

established contacts with businesses and public administration.

Digital transformation is essentially a descendant of the knowledge-based information

society. The first phase of the digital transformation was characterized by finding

solutions in the form of devices, tools and applications that were the right answer

for the needs in the domain of production, preservation, access and management

of knowledge. In this first phase, the design was in the foreground – solutions were

produced that were independent, such as a database, an application, a personal

computer, a smartphone, etc.

Today, however, the focus is not on the individual use of these technological solutions,

but on the connection between devices and systems in a network that is driven by

intelligence and powered by technology.

In essence, in a rapidly developing technological environment, digital transformation

is a kind of driving force in the process of innovation, efficiency and development

in all sectors of social life. Integrating digital technologies into all segments of an

organization fundamentally changes business models, processes and user experiences.

Digital transformation also helps competitiveness, especially through the use of data

DIGITAL ERA - TRANSFORMATION, SECURITY, PROTOCOL, DIPLOMACY, ETIQUETTE

analytics, the so-called "cloud computing", artificial intelligence, and the so called

“Internet of Things (IoT)”.

Along with the benefits, it must be taken into account that the digital era also

brings significant challenges related to security. Our increasing dependence and

interconnectedness with digital systems has opened up new opportunities for

cybercriminals to exploit these vulnerabilities. The increasing number and sophistication

of cyber-attacks are a significant risk for organizations, institutions and individuals,

and therefore when we talk about digital transformation, we must pay considerable

attention to the introduction of security measures.

Why Cyber Security is of great importance?

In the digital era, cyber security plays a key role in protecting digital assets and digital

data. It is composed of a multitude of practices and measures aimed at preventing

unauthorized access, that is, detecting cyber incidents and creating systems resistant

to these challenges. A comprehensive approach to cyber security includes risk analysis,

secure infrastructure design, trained employees and training programs, a response

plan to cyber incidents and risks, as well as cooperation with stakeholders, i.e. various

factors.

Cyber security differs from cyber safety, in that it refers to the protection of persons

from harmful online content and activities, while cyber security refers to the protection

of data and information on information networks.

Organizations must undergo a comprehensive risk analysis in order to properly identify

vulnerabilities and prioritize security investments. This type of approach, which is also

proactive, allows early preparation and mitigation of potential risks in an efficient way.

The implementation of secure hardware and software solutions such as "firewall",

encryption mechanisms and unauthorized access detection systems build the security

of the digital infrastructure against all types of security threats.

With this in mind, what is most likely is that if these systems are set up as intended,

the only way a system can be hacked is through human error. That is why organizations

and institutions must invest enough time and resources to train their employees and

enable those employees to upgrade their knowledge in the future. At the core of those

security initiatives are several key practices such as proper password management

and setting strong passwords, identifying phishing attempts, and being careful with

accessing and sharing sensitive information. Only if there is a cyber-security culture

in an organization, it will be able to minimize the human factor influence in enabling

unauthorized entries into the system.

DigitalTransformation and Cyber Security

The main cyber security risks can be divided into threats and risks. Cyber security

threats include viruses and other harmful software, hacker attacks, misinformation,

identity theft, online fraud and employees, while risks include eradication and

disclosure of important data and documents, business interruption, financial losses,

loss of reputation and violation of legal provisions. According to the basic cyber-

security training for employees in the public administration and employees in the

private sector, employees are a key factor in cyber-security and they have a greater

number of responsibilities such as: responsible behavior, adequate awareness of cyber

risks, reporting incidents and respecting the defined protection measures.

Every minute, about half a million attacks can be seen in cyberspace, and threats and

cybercrime take different forms – from "Denial of Service" attacks, all the way to theft,

blackmail, extortion, manipulation and eradication. The tools are also different and can

include malware, spyware, social engineering, and even changes to physical systems

(Sotiroski, 2018).

Professor Ljupco Sotiroski in "Protection of cyber-security and implementation of the

legal framework", says that as the threats are very numerous and different, so are

the opportunities - technology constantly gives us new ideas, new products and new

ways to live life. Technology presents us with new economic opportunities, new ways of

conducting business, etc.

Cyber hygiene is also an important element of cyber security. Cyber hygiene is

essentially a word for practices that can be applied to increase cyber security and safety

in an organization. Practices for implementing cyber hygiene can be: clean desk, clean

screen, strong password and changing it constantly, physical security of premises,

documents, devices and systems, caution when opening links, updating software,

upgrading hardware and equipment , data backup and antivirus usage. In terms of who

DIGITAL ERA - TRANSFORMATION, SECURITY, PROTOCOL, DIPLOMACY, ETIQUETTE

implements these practices, employees are responsible for a clean desk, clean screen,

strong password, physical security of premises, documents, devices and systems, and

caution when opening links, while information technology takes care of automated

changing passwords, updating software, backing up data, using antivirus, and upgrading

hardware and equipment. An example of these practices is - a strong password that

should be more than 10 characters long, be complex with letters, numbers and special

characters, as well as memorable, or in other words, phrases should be used.

Data privacy and data protection

It is quite logical that when a system collects a huge amount of data in a short period of

time, a huge amount of which is personal data, the security of that data and preventing

it from being stolen and misused becomes a top priority. Privacy regulation such as

the General Data Protection Regulation of the European Union, which is "de facto"

also law in the EU and the European Economic Community, and is also a component

in the Privacy Act and the Human Rights Act in the EU, establishes the responsible

use of data in order to protect the privacy of each person. In addition, compliance with

data protection regulations is not only a legal obligation, but also a way to build trust

between stakeholders.

The role of artificial intelligence in relation to security

Artificial intelligence has emerged as a powerful tool in the development of cyber

security capabilities. Artificial intelligence algorithms can detect threads and anomalies

in vast amounts of data, helping to identify potential security threats in cyberspace.

Machine learning algorithms "de facto" learn from each new cyber incident, so with

each passing day they are better and faster in detecting possible problems and security

threats in cyberspace. In addition, security solutions based on artificial intelligence

enable real-time monitoring, automated threat detection and rapid incident response,

thus improving the position of the organization in the context of its cyber security

capabilities.

What remains open, in the context of the use of artificial intelligence in cyber security,

is for each individual or organization to ensure that it is used in an ethical and morally

correct manner. Attacks by hostile groups whose goal is exactly artificial intelligence

systems in which they themselves have been manipulated, represent a huge challenge.

It is certainly worth mentioning that AI algorithms can lead to unfair and discriminatory

results and therefore organizations must very carefully determine the ethical

implications and potential risks associated with artificial intelligence and at the same

time adopt a set of measures that will respond to these elements accordingly.

DigitalTransformation and Cyber Security

Building trust and resilience

The development according to the process of digital transformation leads to the fact

that organizations must prioritize the building of trust and resilience. Changing people's

minds and prioritizing cyber security considerations are very important at every stage

of digital transformation. Organizations, in turn, must introduce a certain type of cyber

security culture, where employees are educated and encouraged to take responsibility

for maintaining best practices in this regard.

Constant testing and upgrading of security measures is vital in maintaining the level

of preparedness, especially considering the threats that increase and evolve every day.

Incident response plans, mentioned above, must be put into operation, that is, they

must be tested, people must be familiar with them and they must be used according

to needs. The protocols in these plans are mainly about detecting, containing and

recovering from any cyber attack as soon as possible. In that context, the need for

cooperation and sharing of information between actors in the security sphere and

industry, other organizations, government entities and the like is extremely important,

i.e. between all stakeholders who can strengthen the collective defense against cyber

threats.

Cyber security in North Macedonia

National Cyber Security Strategy

The first National Cyber Security Strategy was adopted in 2018 (for the period 2018-

2022) and it indicates that cyber defense is an autonomous and specific branch in

the broader concept of cyber security. The current National Cyber Security Strategy

of North Macedonia is a more extensive document from December 2022, and for the

period 2023-2027. This document, as stated, "enables a safe, resilient and reliable

digital environment that makes the Republic of North Macedonia a safe place for online

activities and work, with developed capacities and the ability to protect and promote

national interests in and through cyberspace".

DIGITAL ERA - TRANSFORMATION, SECURITY, PROTOCOL, DIPLOMACY, ETIQUETTE

The new National Strategy is divided into 5 separate parts:

1. An introduction to the issue with special emphasis on the priority of strengthened

cyber-security at the national level, as a basic element for economic growth and

prosperity and of vital importance for national security.

2. Methodology for the development of the ITU national cyber security strategy and

the ENISA guidelines and tools.

3. Principles of Cyber Security (Cyber Security is Everyone's Responsibility; Cooperation

and Support; Cyber Security by Design; Cyber Security as a Driver; Prioritization Based

on Risk Level; Broad Security; International Diplomacy.

4. Vision and five priority actions, i.e. pillars: creation and improvement of national

capacities for cyber security; security and resilience of critical infrastructure and

national information and communication systems; a society resilient to cyber threats;

minimizing the impact of incidents in cyberspace; and national and international

cooperation.

5. Review of new technologies as challenges for cyber security.

The Strategy itself has been developed with a comprehensive approach from multiple

stakeholders in a process that consists of five separate phases, as follows:

• initial phase (initiation) with a focus on processes, timelines and identification of key

stakeholders, in order to develop a strategy development plan;

• second phase or analysis aimed at assessing the National Strategy for Cyber Security

2018-2022 and analyzing the national space of cyber security taking into account the

reports from the USAID cyber risk preparedness program;

• third phase – preparation of the National Cyber Security Strategy;

• fourth phase – implementation of the national strategy, for which it is considered

that the key element is the structural approach in the implementation, supported by

appropriate human and financial resources.

• fifth phase or monitoring and evaluation of whether the Strategy is being implemented

as intended, ie assessment of whether it is still relevant, whether it reflects the

Government's goals and whether certain adjustments are needed.

DigitalTransformation and Cyber Security

Figure 1: The five stages in the process of developing the National Cyber Security

Strategy of the Republic of North Macedonia

The national strategy establishes a vision, which is "enabling a safe, resilient, reliable

digital environment that makes the Republic of North Macedonia a safe place for online

activity and work".

This vision, as stated above, devides into 5 pillars with several development goals each

described in the figure below.

Figure 2: The five pillars on which the National Cyber Security Strategy of the Republic of

North Macedonia and their goals rests

DIGITAL ERA - TRANSFORMATION, SECURITY, PROTOCOL, DIPLOMACY, ETIQUETTE

Regarding the first pillar, Building and improving national cyber security capacities,

it is indicated that each country must prioritize its capabilities for technical and

operational detection and response to cyber security incidents, so that it can cope

with the changing environment and increasing threats. As the strategy says, technical,

human and financial resources are needed that are in close cooperation with their

counterparts from other national and EU-level bodies, the public sector, private

companies and the research community.

The first goal – developing a clear cyber security management structure indicates that

the Government of the Republic of North Macedonia intends to take the leading role

in the cyber security domain to help organizations and citizens recognize the value of

cyber security and to support the efforts of the state for the overall raising of awareness

and the level of cyber security. In this domain, the promotion of a National Cyber

Security Policy is also planned, through the development of a regulatory framework

and the encouragement of a structure that unites and coordinates all institutions and

stakeholders that have responsibilities in the domain of cyber security.

The second goal – establishing a body with operational capacities for cyber security

indicates that the state must adapt its capacities and capabilities at the operational

and technical level for detecting and reacting to cyber incidents. This should be

implemented through the National Cyber Security Authority which will provide support

for responding to serious cyber security incidents. This body will detect and evaluate

security incidents that may affect or influence the government network and national

information and communication systems. This body would also be the national cyber

security authority. The body would certainly have close cooperation with all other

state and non-state actors within the framework of cyber security, with MKD – CIRT

(National Centre for Computer Incident Response), critical information infrastructure

sectors, operators of essential services and other capacities in this domain. As key

activities under this objective, the Strategy defines: the drafting and adoption of the

Law on Security of Networks and Information Systems, which will transpose the NIS

Directive; establishment of the national body for cyber security; and creation of a

technical-operational plan for the functioning of the national body for cyber security.

The third goal – increased capabilities for defense operations in cyber space points to

the fact that in order to conduct effective cyber operations, adequate cyber defense

capabilities must be developed. One of the steps in this direction is the establishment

of a National Institute for Cyber Security and Digital Forensics whose function would

be education, re-education and training of cyber professionals at the government level,

the public administration and other stakeholders who need this type of education.

DigitalTransformation and Cyber Security

The fourth goal – establishment of an institute for cyber security and digital forensics

refers to the establishment of this institute with support and in coordination with

academic institutions in the country, as well as with other public and private institutions

in the domain of cyber security. The main mission of this institute would be continuous

monitoring and identification of challenges in cyberspace and implementation of

curricula and trainings in order to strengthen the capacities to deal with them. The

institute planned in this objective should cover the following areas: academic education

of all three cycles of studies, continuous training of cyber professionals and research

and development

The expected results of the creation of the Institute are the following:

✓ created programs for the academic community;

✓ created programs for the training of cyber professionals;

✓ creation of profiles of cyber professionals and appropriate courses/trainings, by

which they will achieve the appropriate level;

✓ implemented programs/courses for academic education and training of cyber

professionals;

✓ progressive growth of trained persons;

✓ participation in international projects and activities;

✓ creation of a regional center for cyber security;

✓ cooperation with foreign academic institutions.

Regarding the second pillar – security and resilience of critical infrastructure and

national information and communication systems, it should be noted that the strategic

objective is to encourage the implementation of a coherent and comprehensive national

framework for policies, procedures and technical standards that help ensure more

resilient network with protection of public information and their systems and services.

The first goal in the second pillar – secure and resilient critical information infrastructure,

refers to the critical ICT infrastructure that includes information systems and network

infrastructure, which in the event of their interruption or destruction can cause serious

consequences for the health, safety, economic well-being of citizens, or the efficient

functioning of government and the economy. Within this goal, several key activities

have been defined, namely: definition and acceptance of minimum technical and

organizational measures for cyber security, by sector; creation of sectoral CIRT and

SOC structures; establishing procedures for exchanging information on threats and

incidents in the sectors; promoting cooperation by organizing technical exercises

and scenarios for dealing with threats and incidents in critical sectors; procedures for

storing and protecting data that are processed in the Information Infrastructure and

Important Information systems; implementation of measures to ensure operational

DIGITAL ERA - TRANSFORMATION, SECURITY, PROTOCOL, DIPLOMACY, ETIQUETTE

continuity and recovery from disasters and implementation of a mechanism for cyber

security compliance with national and international requirements.

The second goal in this pillar, according to the Strategy, refers to strengthening

and improving the security of information systems and networks. Digitization, as

mentioned earlier, is essential for a modern society, a modern administration and

efficient government services for citizens. The strategy states that the management of

information security in the public sector is based on the Law on electronic governance

and electronic services and its by-laws, while the Law on the Protection of Personal

Data establishes the principles and technical and organizational measures to be taken

for processing security of personal data in the public and private sectors. Key activities

in this goal are the definition of a minimum set of technological and organizational

measures for cyber security; the adoption of a national level framework for risk

management; and a concept for the implementation and verification of the minimum

set of technological and organizational measures for cyber security.

The third objective refers to the establishment of partnership and cooperation

between state and private capacities through public private partnership. In relation to

this goal, the Strategy states that the Government, the private sector, the research

community and society as a whole, which are essentially the targets of cyber attacks,

need technical information if they want to detect these attacks and act on them. It

should be known that this type of information can be obtained through analyses, while

analyzes can only be prepared by professionals – providers of ICT security services or

operators in critical infrastructure. The strategy says that cooperation is extremely

important because through the exchange of data and information in an efficient and

effective way, it is possible to influence the reduction or prevention of damages that

can result from cyber attacks. This cooperation applies to all levels – or, information

about certain threats, raising awareness, creating experts in the field and creating a

safe cyberspace. The key activities from the aspect of this goal are – strategic planning

of government activities; development of procedures and processes for public-private

partnership; and improving the management of the development of public-private

partnerships in the field of cyber security.

The third pillar – a society resistant to cyber threats indicates that the increased use,

and therefore the dependence on technology and the little knowledge of the challenges

that exist in the cyber space brings the need for the development of measures and

activities that will increase the resistance of the entire society to the challenges after

cyber security. This means that it is necessary to implement programs and activities

in the educational system to increase awareness of cyber security; then implement

programs and activities to increase awareness of these threats among employees in

DigitalTransformation and Cyber Security

the public and private sectors, as well as among the entire population; and to implement

activities for the development of programs for the education of cyber professionals who

will be able to deal with advanced and complex attacks and challenges in cyberspace.

The first goal of the third pillar – increasing awareness of cyber space, according to the

Strategy, is a basic prerequisite for more effective protection against cyber risks. Most

of the users do not know or do not practice the basic security rules, as it is mentioned

in the Strategy. According to the Strategy, it is essential to promote a healthy cyber

security culture that provides all actors with the necessary awareness and confidence

to maximize the benefits of the information society and minimize the possibility of

exposure to cyberspace risks. The key activities within this goal according to the Strategy

are: creation of programs to increase awareness of cyber security among students in

primary and secondary schools; incorporation of cyber security concepts and thematic

units in primary and secondary education curricula; development and distribution of

educational materials according to the target groups; educating and training teaching

staff in elementary and secondary schools in the field of cyber security and providing

appropriate and modern materials for students; creation of publicly available courses,

multimedia campaigns and media coverage in order to reach a larger population; and

providing adequate education and training in the field of cyber security for employees

in the public and private sectors.

The second goal in the third pillar refers to the development and implementation

of cyber educational programs and trainings, which is an extremely important goal

considering that the Strategy establishes that the existing curricula in all cycles and

studies of the universities in the country are not aligned and do not fully meet the

needs to educate and train professionals in the field of cyber security. This goal also

foresees several measures that will help in the establishment of programs for education,

further education and practical exercises and trainings for cyber professionals, namely:

improvement of existing and development of new university curricula in order to create

appropriate personnel in the field of cyber security; inclusion of cyber security elements

in all university study programs; attraction, education, re-education and training of

cyber professionals from the public sector and other constituents who need this type

of training; participation in national and international research projects and activities

related to cyber security; and supporting research facilities and business innovation

through scientific research centers in the field of cyber security.

The fourth pillar – minimizing the impact of incidents in cyber space indicates

that incidents in cyber space occur daily and that with each passing day, they gain

momentum. Strengthening incident response and management capabilities across

organizations, minimizing the potential damage that can be caused, and providing

DIGITAL ERA - TRANSFORMATION, SECURITY, PROTOCOL, DIPLOMACY, ETIQUETTE

better support are essential to building a healthy cyberspace, as stipulated in the

Strategy. Additionally, this Strategy indicates that these ultimate results can be

achieved by taking appropriate and proportionate measures to prevent and minimize

the impact of incidents in the security of networks and information and communication

systems; through appropriate and proportionate technical and organizational

measures to manage the risks related to the security of the network and information

and communication systems; by notifying the relevant competent authorities of

any incident that has a substantial impact on their services, as well as by improved

coordination between stakeholders in dealing with incidents.

The first goal of the fourth pillar – timely and appropriate response to attacks

and incidents related to cyber space indicates a whole process and system by which

these attacks will be first noticed, reported, analyzed and there will be an appropriate

response to them. Cooperation between the National Computer Incident Response

Center MKD-CIRT and the Ministry of Interior will be improved by establishing a single

point for reporting incidents and crimes in cyberspace. The adoption of a legal solution

that will introduce and regulate the mandatory reporting of incidents and attacks

by the public sector and certain sectors of the critical information infrastructure

will also have a positive impact. The national categorization of cyber incidents and

the prioritization of their resolution will help towards a timely and quality response,

and the timely identification and response to incidents also depend on the process

of establishing quality and equipped operational CSIRT teams in critical sectors. It

is extremely important to establish a set of rules and principles for cooperation and

exchange of information, support during response and coordination in dealing with

incidents, as well as the implementation of mechanisms for detection and rapid

response to cyber incidents in organizations - state administration bodies and the

Information Infrastructure operators.

The second goal is the recommendations for the use of security technology in society,

which states that the establishment of a safe society by using the possibilities of

digital technologies, artificial intelligence, quantum technologies and electronic

communications is the best way to ensure adequate protection against cyber threats..

The third objective – managing and monitoring risks and threats indicates that the

continuous cooperation between the public and private sectors and the Information

Infrastructure sectors leads to a better understanding, prioritization and management

of cyber risks as well as by identifying risks and threats that cover one or more critical

sectors. This goal includes continuous assessment and management of cyber risks,

then supporting the private sector in assessment and management of cyber risks by

providing assessment guidelines based on international standards and education of

DigitalTransformation and Cyber Security

legal entities through appropriate training, as well as the adoption of a National a cyber

risk assessment framework to be used in both the public and private sectors. This is

followed by the establishment of a register of identified information assets that are of

great importance for the state.

The fourth objective refers to the timely and appropriate handling of cybercrime.

According to the analysis, the number of reports from state institutions to the Ministry

of Interior - the Department for Computer Crime and Digital Forensics for identified

computer attacks on the systems has increased significantly, and external and internal

reasons have been defined for the same phenomena:

• external reasons: development of information technology, high degree of use of

information technology in everyday life, significant growth of the digital society

after the Corona virus pandemic, insufficient knowledge of information technology,

and security in this area by users, etc.

• internal reasons: deficiencies in computer security of computer systems in state

institutions, including hospitals, schools, etc. According to the analyses, this is due

to the insufficient staffing of the IT services in the institutions, the employment of

inadequate staff and lack of investment in modern IT technologies.

From the point of view of suppression of computer crime, the Ministry of Interior

identifies these developments, provides support in comparing investigations and

similar, that is, takes the following steps:

✓ coordination with the banking sector;

✓ coordination with the national CIRT in order to define what competences would be

distributed between the Ministry and the CIRT;

✓ coordination with the National Bank for the purpose of data exchange and

cooperation;

✓ coordination with the State Audit Office, ministries and other authorities of the

state;

✓ contact and coordination with international institutions in the field of computer

security - INTERPOL, EUROPOL, Special Tasks Unit;

✓ implementation of an international campaign to improve Interpol's computer

security;

✓ visits and coordination with the computer crime departments in the regional

Sectors of Interior in order to determine the challenges and provide guidelines for

more effective action;

✓ preparation of a new Strategy for computer crime with an emphasis on cooperation

and coordination with other institutions that have competence for dealing with

computer crime; and

DIGITAL ERA - TRANSFORMATION, SECURITY, PROTOCOL, DIPLOMACY, ETIQUETTE

✓ implementation of the Guidelines for providing data from mobile devices in regional

sectors as well as holding training for implementing the steps of the Guidelines.

The fifth pillar refers to national and international cooperation and it indicates that

public institutions should cooperate closely at the international and national level to

enable security in cyberspace. The strategy says the state is also relying on partnerships

with the private sector and international allies to strengthen its cyber resilience. Several

goals arise from this, namely:

The first goal refers to cooperation in the field of cyber security at the national and

international level, where the activities that are defined refer to participation in the

definition of international legal acts related to the manner of behavior in cyber space,

freedom of expression, protection of personal data, privacy rights and fundamental

human rights and freedoms; then the strengthened multilateral cooperation within the

relevant international organizations such as the UN, OSCE, the Council of Europe and

others; the strengthened bilateral cooperation with the member states of NATO and

the European Union; building trust at the international level by creating multifaceted

contact mechanisms; and building strategic partnerships with other countries in order

to strengthen collective action.

The second goal of the fifth pillar refers to the responsible behavior of the state

and the measures for building trust in cyberspace, where the key activities are the

following: further development of the rules, norms and principles of the responsible

behavior of the states and the ways of their implementation and - if it is necessary – to

introduce changes in them or develop additional rules of conduct; maintaining a regular

institutional dialogue with the broad participation of the states under the auspices of

the UN; application of international law for the use of information and communication

technologies by country; building trust measures; and capacity building.

Cyber Defense Strategy of the Ministry of Defense

The cyber defense strategy adopted by the Ministry of Defense in 2020 indicates that

for the state to be able to maintain the values of a democratic society such as the

security of citizens, the protection of sovereignty and territorial integrity, the principles

of democracy and the rule of law, it must build and maintain a complex system of

national defense. From today's perspective, that system is indeed more complex

than ever. Especially significant are the challenges brought by new technologies in

cyberspace, something that is especially visible after the illegal Russian aggression

against independent and sovereign Ukraine. This war showed us that the European

continent in the 21st century is still a fertile ground for conventional warfare, but it also

showed us that today's military doctrine is not limited to conventional weapons, but

DigitalTransformation and Cyber Security

on the contrary, it largely uses cyberspace, for a kind of hybrid warfare. No country is

immune to hybrid threats - and the region, and especially Serbia, Bulgaria, Montenegro,

Albania, and even North Macedonia, were subjected to a series of hybrid attacks - from

attacks on key government systems such as the Health Insurance Fund, to everyday

hybrid threats related to reports of planted bombs in schools, hospitals, institutions.

A cyber defense strategy recognizes that cyber security differs from cyber defense –

and that, it is said, the main difference is the nature and intensity of cyber attacks,

without being able to specify exact and precise criteria.

The readiness of the state to deal with the challenges in the cyber space, or, the

readiness to defend against cyber attacks is complex and comprehensive. Cyber

defense is not only active during emergency and crisis situations, but on the contrary

– it is active daily and constantly. One of the key elements is the building of capacities

and the strengthening of cyber defense within the Ministry of Defense and the Army

of the Republic of North Macedonia, which will be ready to face the challenges in the

cyber space.

According to the Strategy, there are a number of state and non-state actors that can

carry out a cyber attack that would have an impact on the system and activate cyber

defense capabilities. The primary targets of cyber-attacks can be users and systems

that connect the computing environment with the physical infrastructure.

Digital Diplomacy: Functionality of the Global Environment in the Digital Era

An introduction to digital diplomacy

Diplomacy has long been considered the art of conducting negotiations between

nations and a way of developing international relations (Baylis, Owens, & Smith,

2017). Traditionally, diplomacy involves face-to-face meetings, written documentation

and correspondence, and the exchange of official documents. Today, with the rapid

penetration and development of new technologies and new ways of functioning of

societies, the digital age has introduced new ways in which diplomacy also functions.

In the digital age, diplomacy can also be defined as the use of technology and digital tools

in facilitating communications, negotiations

and consensus building between states.

Digital diplomacy also includes the exchange

of information, ideas and policies through

different types of digital channels, including

e-mail, video-conferencing, social networks

and online platforms.

Digital transformation has, in fact, greatly

expanded the scope and reach of diplomacy,

and enabled diplomats to have access to

wider audiences and conduct diplomatic

activities more efficiently and effectively

(Melissen, 2017).

Figure 3: Advantages versus disadvan-

Digital transformation has changed the tages for diplomacy in the digital era

dynamics of international relations as well

as diplomatic practice. One of the most notable changes is the speed and simplicity of

communication. Digital tools have eliminated the constraints of physical distances and

time zones, and have allowed diplomats to talk in real time from one side of the globe

to the other and instantly receive information on a global scale. This, in turn, enables

quick decision-making and an accelerated pace when comparing negotiations of any

type (Fischer-Ontrup, 2019).

The digital era enables another very important benefit, which is the democratization

of diplomacy, by establishing a platform that allows a wider range of stakeholders to

have the opportunity to be involved in diplomatic discourse. Through social networks,

diplomats can very easily establish contact with the public, with organizations from

the non-governmental sector, with non-state actors, and all this allows the diplomatic

DIGITAL ERA - TRANSFORMATION, SECURITY, PROTOCOL, DIPLOMACY, ETIQUETTE

process to be more transparent and inclusive. All this means that diplomacy is more

accessible and open to the interests and concerns of different communities (Slaughter,

2018).

The technology also enabled the development of the so-called data-driven diplomacy,

especially considering that diplomats suddenly have the ability to analyze and gain

insight into global trends, public opinion and policy priorities, precisely using new

technological tools. In this way, diplomats can make real decisions, anticipate changes,

recognize challenges and change diplomatic strategies and tactics according to these

directions. Thus, in a word, diplomacy becomes a science based on facts and evidence,

it is proactive, implements efficient policies and enables a simpler process for ending

conflicts (Bjola & Holmes, 2019).

The digital age has brought both new opportunities and new challenges – especially

in the domain of cyber security and information warfare. Diplomats, if they are to reap

the benefits of technological inventions, must have a way to deal with the complexities

of the cyber domain, ensure that sensitive information is protected, and be proactive

in dealing with the misinformation that societies face on a daily basis. All this requires

the development of a robust cyber security system with its own protocols, while

simultaneously requiring a high degree of digital literacy among diplomats, who now

have to effectively deal with these galloping threats in the digital space (Cavelty, 2020).

In general, the digital age has transformed diplomacy, increased the way we define it,

and redefined its practices. The use of all that today's technology makes possible has

revolutionized communication and inclusiveness, and supported the decision-making

process. The rapid progress of technology, however, has also led to the emergence

of challenges, especially in the context of security in cyberspace, challenges to which

diplomats must adapt, while simultaneously using the potential offered by the new era.

The importance and benefits of digital diplomacy

Digital diplomacy, also known as e-diplomacy or cyber-diplomacy, is the new and

modern approach to diplomatic practice developed over centuries. It is also a vital

tool for governments and international organizations. As stated above, technology

has drastically changed the way we communicate, and thus the face of the global

environment. Simply put, technology has reduced the distance between governments,

diplomats and citizens on a global level and has even enabled direct contact between

them.

A very significant benefit of digital diplomacy and the new era is in the domain of crisis

management and ending conflicts, especially because in times of crisis or conflict,

Digital Diplomacy: Functionality of the Global Environment in the Digital Era

access to fast and accurate information is of crucial importance. Through digital

channels, diplomats receive real-time news, then share information and coordinate

efforts in an efficient manner. Social networks are also an important segment, especially

when it comes to the rapid transfer of information to end users – whether in the form

of instructions to protect life and property, or in terms of guidance for dealing with

potential threats.

Digital diplomacy has also revolutionized cultural exchange, breaking down barriers

between different peoples and cultures. Through online platforms, governments can

present the rich heritage of their countries, their music, art, their traditions to global

audiences. All this not only promotes cultural diversity, but also promotes mutual

understanding and respect. Through these digital platforms, language learning

programs and initiatives in the field of education that lead to a more inclusive and

connected world can be promoted.

The benefits can also be clearly seen in the domain of economic diplomacy and

diplomatic innovation. Through digital platforms, governments can attract foreign

investors, promote tourism, trade, and demonstrate their economic potential. Digital

tools and technologies also offer new innovative solutions for global problems such as

climate change, health challenges, etc. Joint efforts, made possible by online platforms

that serve as a catalyst, enable the development of new policies and procedures aimed

at finding solutions to these issues and challenges.

The main concepts and tools of digital diplomacy

Digital diplomacy includes several tools and concepts that include the characteristics

of this branch of diplomacy.

One of them is public diplomacy, which involves the efforts of governments or

organizations to reach out to foreign audiences in order to build closer relationships

and promote a positive image of their country or organization. Public diplomacy can

also be considered an integral part or segment of strategic communications with the

intention of influencing public opinion and external perception in order to achieve a

specific goal in foreign policy.

DIGITAL ERA - TRANSFORMATION, SECURITY, PROTOCOL, DIPLOMACY, ETIQUETTE

Figure 4: Activities and tools in the domain of public diplomacy

The main purpose of public diplomacy is to promote understanding and trust as well as

goodwill between nations and organizations through the dissemination of information,

closer and more comprehensive cultural exchange and dialogue. It includes various

activities such as cultural exhibitions, educational exchanges, international transmission

of content with a positive impact, public speaking events and implementation of digital

diplomacy through online platforms.

Public diplomacy differs from traditional diplomacy in that it does not primarily refer to

interactions between governments and official representatives, but to the development

of positive relations with non-state actors, organizations from the non-governmental

sector, citizens, media, public opinion makers and the like. Public diplomacy recognizes

the power of public opinion and non-governmental movements in shaping international

relations, and that is precisely why they are its goal.

De facto, public diplomacy plays an extremely significant role in shaping public

perception of the policies, values and culture of a state and nation. It can increase a

state's "soft power" and its power to influence through persuasion as opposed to

coercion. By promoting dialogue, understanding and mutual respect, public diplomacy

creates bridges that connect different cultures, resolves misunderstandings and

promotes closer relations between countries.

Digital Diplomacy: Functionality of the Global Environment in the Digital Era

Social networks such as Facebook, Twitter, Instagram and LinkedIn also have a great

impact on digital diplomacy, especially as diplomats use these platforms to promote

opinions, ideas and policies and initiate discussions with their followers. Communications

with diplomats simply have no boundaries, except for the standards of diplomatic

practice and etiquette. Most often, this type of interactions and dialogue can be seen

in the relations between diplomats and representatives of the media, experts or the

so-called. "influencers".

Another form or tool of digital diplomacy is the so-called "digital storytelling", because

the digital sphere leaves a huge space for telling a perfect story about one's country,

culture or nation. The digital space allows the use of multimedia content such as photos,

videos, infographics, podcasts, blogs and etc., with the help of which enticing and visually

supported narratives can be developed that evoke emotion and temptation. Digital

storytelling is another more comprehensive way to promote diplomatic messages that

hold the audience's attention and interest.

E-diplomacy, seen as a tool, essentially describes the way in which diplomatic practice

is realized through new technologies. It includes tools for the organization of on-line

negotiations, digital conferences, virtual summits or secure conference connections for

the transfer of sensitive information.

One extremely important tool for diplomats is the ability to analyze the vast amount

of information available in cyberspace. In this way, diplomats can get a picture of

public opinion at home and in any foreign country and accordingly change or shape

their diplomatic strategies, identify stakeholders, maximize the effect of messages and

most effectively target specific key audiences.

On-line campaigns are another strategic tool of diplomats, especially when it comes to

targeted policy promotion, dealing with misinformation and raising public awareness

of certain specific issues. Diplomatic missions can engage in campaigns on social

networks, in various on-line petitions or various local or smaller movements that can

have a national effect – all with the aim of gaining even greater public support.

Diplomacy training conducted online is a tool that is important for digital diplomacy,

considering the efficiency and speed in conducting this type of training. These programs

include online courses, webinars, and virtual workshops covering various aspects of

digital diplomacy, including social media management, cyberspace communication

strategies, or crisis management.

DIGITAL ERA - TRANSFORMATION, SECURITY, PROTOCOL, DIPLOMACY, ETIQUETTE

The role of social networks in diplomacy

With the development of mass media and mass communication, social networks have

rapidly transformed not only our social lives, but also political relationships. What is

clearly noticeable is that in this modern era, political leaders and diplomats at the

global level are increasingly using social networks to convey a certain political message,

to signal a certain political intention or to connect with a certain foreign politician. If

in a certain situation traditional (face-to-face) diplomacy is limited, social networks

can be extremely significant in opening dialogue and developing trust between states.

In essence, if an analysis is made of the way officials behave on social networks, it is

easy to come to the conclusion that their messages sent through these networks are

consistent and within the framework of how one state wants to be recognized on the

international stage.

One illustration of this is Twitter's role in reaching of the Iran nuclear deal framework.

After the termination of diplomatic relations between the United States and Iran in

1980, the potential for high-profile diplomatic interactions was very small, therefore the

successful adoption of the Iran nuclear deal framework in 2015 was a surprise, which in

a certain percentage should attribute its success to the social Twitter network. Namely,

the way in which this social network was used by the official Iranian representatives,

made it possible to create a positive climate that foreshadowed a shift from hostile

positions, reconstruction of the narratives between the two countries and, accordingly,

the introduction of new negotiating positions.

What can be drawn as a conclusion regarding the way countries are represented on social

networks is that it is mostly in a way that protects the state identity, it is affirmative and

can have a direct impact on the possibilities and potential of foreign policy.

Figure 5: Characteristics of social networks relevant to digital diplomacy

Digital Diplomacy: Functionality of the Global Environment in the Digital Era

Social networks can also be seen as a double-edged sword – they are a channel for the

instant transfer of opinions and ideas, an effective tool for global communication, while

at the same time they can extremely quickly damage the reputation of a particular

country or person. After all, the USA and the White House during the time of President

Trump is one example of how (again) Twitter has shaped world politics, in one way or

another. It was under the leadership of Trump and his "Twitter diplomacy" that numerous

discussions between high-profile figures were conducted on this platform, and that too

in front of the watchful eye of the public. It could be seen with the Mexican president

Vicente Fox (around the construction of the border wall), the declarations of nuclear war

with the North Korean leader Kim Jong Un – examples that showed the lack of tact in

the foreign policy of the world superpower. Therefore, the use of this social network by

President Trump also showed the other side of the coin, that is, how much social networks

can delegitimize a certain person,

and how much they can have a

destructive effect and increase the

void created by the loss of trust in

international relations.

This can also be seen in the way

American-Chinese relations are

developing through social networks.

The fighting spirit that China's

foreign minister, Wang Yi, allegedly

demanded from his diplomats can

be clearly seen in several cases –

for example, the protests in Hong

Kong, when the profiles of Chinese

diplomats could be seen with the

so-called . "whataboutism" that

positions the United States as

unjust, inhumane and hypocritical,

through the issues and problems

that exist in American society

such as racial discrimination or

gun violence. Such (un)diplomatic

attitude was also evident in

President Trump's announcements

showing that while social Figure 6: An example of former US

networks have facilitated President Donald Trump's Twitter

diplomacy

DIGITAL ERA - TRANSFORMATION, SECURITY, PROTOCOL, DIPLOMACY, ETIQUETTE

communications, they have largely replaced carefully prepared press statements with

opinions and views that lack the refinement that can have a long-term impact.

It can therefore be said that the transformative power of social networks in world politics

is clear but under-examined. These new platforms are changing the ways in which a

state identifies itself and shapes its foreign policy. In the context of social networks,

one crucial question remains to be answered – how can we harness the potential of

these platforms, which are enormous, while simultaneously nullifying the possibilities

of their negative impact?

If the operational risks of using social platforms are taken into account (without the

obvious political influences), they can be divided into:

1. Information Integrity: Fake news and misinformation on social media spreads at the

speed of light. All world governments face the challenge of dealing with disinformation

and positioning themselves as a credible source of information. It was also clearly visible

during the corona-virus pandemic, when very often official information on social networks

was overlapped with misinformation and misinformation of any type and nature.

2. Security Challenges: Diplomats and Governments must ensure the security of their

social media accounts in order to prevent hacking or unauthorized access. In 2017, the

US Department of Defense's Twitter account was hacked, leading to unauthorized

tweets that had the potential to become a security risk.

3. Diplomatic Protocol: Maintaining diplomatic protocol on social media can be a

challenge in itself. Any incident through social networks can lead to a cooling of

bilateral foreign relations between two countries. Such an example can be found in the

diplomatic disagreements between Canada and Saudi Arabia on Twitter in 2018/9.

4. Overreliance on social networks: although it is clear that social networks offer an

extremely large reach in the transmission of messages, it must be taken into account

that their effectiveness is also limited, especially when it comes to the segment of the

population that has limited access to the Internet and relatively low media literacy.

Therefore, Governments must have a dual approach and never direct their diplomatic

activity only through digital channels, but share balanced narratives, messages and

positions in a traditional way that allows them to reach the widest possible audience.

5. Balancing transparency and classification of information: diplomats must find

a balance between the need to share information and the preservation of certain

information as classified. Today, this is made possible by several platforms like Signal

or Whats App, which enable encrypted communication.

Глава II · Дипломатија во дигиталната ера
Chapter II · Diplomacy in the Digital Era

On-line кампањите се уште една стратешка алатка на дипломатите, особено кога

станува збор за таргетирано промовирање на политики, за справување со дезин-

формации и за подигнување на свесноста кај јавноста за одредени специфични

прашања. Дипломатските мисии можат да се вклучат во кампањи на социјалните

мрежи, во различни on-line петиции или различни локални или помали движења

кои можат да имаат национален ефект – и сето тоа со цел добивање на уште пого-

лема јавна поддршка.

Обуките за дипломатија спроведени on-line, се алатка која е од значење за диги-

талната дипломатија, имајќи ја предвид ефикасноста и брзината во спроведување-

то на ваков вид на обуки. Овие програми вклучуваат on-line курсеви, вебинари и

виртуелни работилници кои покриваат различни аспекти од дигиталната диплома-

тија, вклучувајќи и менаџирањето на социјалните мрежи, комуникациските страте-

гии во сајбер-просторот или кризниот менаџмент.

Улогата на социјалните мрежи во дипломатијата

Со развојот на мас-медиумите и мас-комуникацијата, социјалните мрежи рапидно

ги трансформираа не само нашите социјални животи, туку и политичките односи

и релации. Она што е јасно забележливо е дека во оваа модерна ера, политичките

лидери и дипломатите на глобално ниво сè повеќе ги користат социјалните мрежи

за да пренесат одредена политичка порака, да сигнализираат одредена политичка

намера или да се поврзат со одреден странски политичар. Доколку во одредена

ситуација традиционалната (лице-в-лице) дипломатија е лимитирана, социјалните

мрежи можат да бидат исклучително значајни во отворањето на дијалог и развојот

на довербата помеѓу државите. Во суштина, доколку се изврши анализа на начи-

нот на кој се однесуваат официјалните лица на социјалните мрежи, лесно се доаѓа

до заклучок дека нивните пораки упатени преку овие мрежи се конзистентни и во

рамката на тоа како една змеја сака да биде препознаена на меѓународната сцена.

Една илустрација за тоа е улогата на Twitter во донесувањето на иранскиот нукле-

арен договор. По прекинувањето на дипломатските односи помеѓу САД и Иран во

1980 година, потенцијалот за високо-профилни дипломатски интеракции бил мно-

гу мал, па затоа успешното донесување на Иранскиот нуклеарен договор во 2015

година претставуваше изненадување кое во одреден процент својот успех треба

да го припише и на социјалната мрежа Twitter. Имено, токму начинот на кој била

користена оваа социјална мрежа од страна на официјалните ирански претставни-

ци, овозможила да се создаде позитивна клима која навестувала поместување

од непријателските позиции, реконструирање на наративите помеѓу двете земји и

според тоа воведување на нови преговарачки позиции.

Дигитална дипломатија: функционалност на глобалното опкружување во дигиталната ера

Она што може да се извлече како заклучок во однос на начинот на кој се претста-

вуваат земјите на социјалните мрежи е дека тоа е најчесто на начин кој го штити

државниот идентитет, истиот е афирмативен и може да има директно влијание врз

можностите и потенцијалот на надворешната политика.

Слика 5: Карактеристики на социјалните мрежи од важност за дигиталната дипломатија

На социјалните мрежи може да се гледа и како на нож со две острици – тие се ка-

нал за инстантен трансфер на мислења и идеи, ефикасна алатка за глобална ко-

муникација, додека истовремено тие можат исклучително брзо да и наштетат на

репутацијата на одредена земја или личност. Впрочем, токму САД и Белата куќа во

времето на претседателот Трамп е еден пример за тоа како (повторно) Twitter ја

обликуваше светската политика, на еден или на друг начин. Токму под водство на

Трамп и неговата „Twitter дипломатија“, многубројни дискусии помеѓу високо-про-

филни лица беа водени на оваа платформа, и тоа пред будното око на јавноста. Тоа

можеше да се види со мексиканскиот претседател Висенте Фокс (околу изградбата

на граничниот ѕид), декларациите за нуклеарна војна со севернокорејскиот лидер

Ким Јонг Ун – примери кои го покажуваа недостатокот на такт во надворешната

политика на светската суперсила. Затоа користењето на оваа социјална мрежа од

страна на претседателот Трамп ја покажа и другата страна на паричката, односно

колку социјалните мрежи можат да делегитимизираат одредена личност, колку тие

можат да влијаат деструктивно и да ја зголемат празнината која се создава преку

губење на довербата во меѓународните односи.

Затоа може да се каже дека трансформациската сила на социјалните мрежи во

светската политика е јасна, но недоволно испитана. Овие нови платформи ги мену-

ваат начините на кои една држава се идентификува себе си и ја обликува својата

надворешна политика. Во контекст на социјалните мрежи, останува да се одговори

на едно круцијално прашање – како можеме да ги искористиме потенцијалите на

овие платформи кои се огромни, додека истовремено ги анулираме можностите за

нивно негативно влијание?

Дигитална дипломатија: функционалност на глобалното опкружување во дигиталната ера

Доколку предвид се земат оперативните ризици од користењето на социјалните

платформи (без евидентните политички влијанија), истите можат да се поделат на:

1. Интегритет на информациите: Лажните вести и дезинформациите на социјал-

ните мрежи се шират со брзина на светлината. Сите светски влади се соочуваат со

предизвикот да се носат со дезинформациите и да се позиционираат себе си како

кредибилен извор на информации. Тоа беше јасно видливо и за време на панде-

мијата на корона-вирусот, кога многу често официјалните информации на социјал-

ните мрежи беа поклопувани со мисинформации и дезинформации од секаков тип

и природа.

2. Безбедносни предизвици: Дипломатите и Владите мораат да ја осигураат безбед-

носта на нивните профили на социјалните мрежи, со цел да превенираат хакирање

или неавторизирани влезови. Во 2017 година, Твитер-профилот на Департманот

за одбрана на САД беше хакиран, што доведе до испишување на неавторизирани

твитови кои имаа потенцијал да прераснат во безбедносен ризик.

3. Дипломатски протокол: одржувањето на дипломатски протокол на социјални-

те мрежи може само по себе да биде предизвик. Секоја случка преку социјалните

мрежи може да доведе до заладување на билатералните надворешни односи по-

меѓу две земји. Таков пример може да се најде во дипломатските несогласувања

помеѓу Канада и Саудиска Арабија на Твитер во 2018/9 година.

4. Преголемо ослонување на социјалните мрежи: иако е јасно дека социјалните

мрежи нудат исклучително голем дострел во пренесувањето на пораките, мора да

се има предвид дека и нивната ефикасност е лимитирана, особено ако стане збор

за сегментот од популацијата кој има лимитиран пристап на интернет и релативно

ниска медиумска писменост. Затоа, Владите мораат да имаат дуален пристап и ни-

когаш нивната дипломатска активност да не ја насочуваат единствено преку диги-

талните канали, туку балансирано наративите, пораките и позициите да ги споде-

луваат и на традиционален начин кој овозможува истите да стигнат до најширока

можна публика.

5. Балансирање на транспарентноста и класифицираноста на информациите: ди-

пломатите мораат да најдат баланс помеѓу потребата за споделување на инфор-

мации и зачувување на одредени информации како класифицирани. Денеска тоа е

овозможено од страна на неколку платформи како Signal или Whats App, кои овоз-

можуваат енкриптирана комуникација.

Студии на случај – успешно промовирање на дипломатски кам-

пањи преку социјалните мрежи

Постојат повеќе успешни on-line дипломатски кампањи кои имаа позитивно влија-

ние и покажаа на кој начин може да се искористи потенцијалот на социјалните

мрежи. Една од нив е т.н. „Travel Ban Response“ кампања на канадската влада во

2017 година, која дојде како еден вид на одговор на забраната за патување која ја

воведе САД кон неколку доминантно муслимански земји. Кампањата која имаше

позитивен одек, се развиваше под „хаштагот“ #WelcomeToCanada, а таргетирани

беа социјалната мрежа Твитер и други социјални мрежи. Овој „хаштаг“ беше кори-

стен и од канадскиот премиер Џастин Трудо, кој споделуваше пораки за поддршка

кон оние кои беа опфатени со забраната за патување, додека истовремено ја по-

тенцираше посветеноста на Канада кон инклузија и почитување на различностите.

Кампањата достигна вирално ниво, а истата беше проследена со големо медиум-

ско внимание и позитивни реакции на глобално ниво. „Хаштагот“ беше екстензивно

користен и од Канаѓаните, но и низ целиот свет и тоа најчесто за пренесување на

лични стории и приказни кои ја потврдуваат сликата за мултикултурна Канада која

ги почитува сите луѓе без оглед на раса, нација, религиозна определба.

Дигитална дипломатија: функционалност на глобалното опкружување во дигиталната ера

ска перспектива. Оваа кампања ги вклучи социјалните мрежи Твитер, Facebook и

YouTube, каде беа споделувани пораки со квалитетни визуелизации како инфо-

графици, видеа, лични тестимонијали, со повеќејазичен пристап, говорејќи дирек-
